**Jarvis:** #!/bin/bash
# DigitalOcean VPS Heartbeat Monitor
# Pings Mike via Telegram every 5 minutes with DO VPS health status
# Created: 2026-01-30 | Server: factorylm-prod (DigitalOcean Atlanta)

TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN="8387943893:AAEynugW3SP1sWs6An4aNgZParSSRBlWSJk"
TELEGRAM_CHAT_ID="8445149012"

# Get uptime
UPTIME=$(uptime -p)

# Check services
check_service() {
    if systemctl is-active --quiet "$1" 2>/dev/null; then
        echo "‚úÖ"
    else
        echo "‚ùå"
    fi
}

check_docker() {
    if docker ps 2>/dev/null | grep -q "$1"; then
        echo "‚úÖ"
    else
        echo "‚ùå"
    fi
}

# Service status
CLAWDBOT=$(check_service "clawdbot")
DOCKER=$(check_service "docker")

# Docker containers
CMMS=$(check_docker "atlas-cmms")
MAUTIC=$(check_docker "mautic")
N8N=$(check_docker "n8n")
POSTGRES=$(check_docker "postgres")
REDIS=$(check_docker "redis")

# Memory
MEM_USED=$(free -h | awk '/^Mem:/ {print $3}')
MEM_TOTAL=$(free -h | awk '/^Mem:/ {print $2}')

# Disk
DISK_USED=$(df -h / | awk 'NR==2 {print $5}')

# CPU Load
LOAD=$(cat /proc/loadavg | awk '{print $1}')

# Tailscale IP
TS_IP=$(tailscale ip -4 2>/dev/null || echo "N/A")

# Build message
MESSAGE="üíô *DO Heartbeat* (Atlanta)

‚è± ${UPTIME}
üñ• CPU: ${LOAD} | RAM: ${MEM_USED}/${MEM_TOTAL} | Disk: ${DISK_USED}
üåê Tailscale: ${TS_IP}

*Services:*
${CLAWDBOT} Clawdbot
${DOCKER} Docker

*Containers:*

**Mike H:** Does this project incorporate a digital twin?
[message_id: 3800]

---

**Jarvis:** **Currently: No.** We have an AI assistant, not a digital twin.

**What we have:**
- LLM that answers maintenance questions
- CMMS for work orders
- Synthetic users generating training data
- Knowledge base of Q&A pairs

**What a digital twin would add:**
- Real-time virtual model of actual equipment
- Live PLC data ‚Üí virtual replica
- Simulate failures before they happen
- "What if I change this parameter?" testing
- Predictive maintenance from sensor trends

**Easy path to digital twin:**
```
PLC Modbus data ‚Üí InfluxDB ‚Üí Grafana (visual twin)
                         ‚Üì
                    LLM context

### What You Already Have

| Component | Status | Purpose |

## üöÄ THE SOLUTION: "Jarvis Node" on Each Laptop

### Architecture

```

| Tool | Why Skip |
|------|----------|

**My recommendation - simpler v1:**

```python
# jarvis_node.py - LEAN VERSION
from fastapi import FastAPI
import subprocess
import mss
import base64
import pyautogui  # For clicks/typing (simpler than OpenAdapt)

app = FastAPI()

@app.post("/shell")
def shell(cmd: str):
    return subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True, capture_output=True).stdout

@app.get("/screenshot")
def screenshot():
    with mss.mss() as sct:
        img = sct.grab(sct.monitors[0])
        return base64.b64encode(mss.tools.to_png(img.rgb, img.size))

@app.post("/click")
def click(x: int, y: int):
    pyautogui.click(x, y)
    return {"clicked": [x, y]}

@app.post("/type")
def type_text(text: str):
    pyautogui.write(text)
    return {"typed": text}
```

summary: "Nodes: pairing, capabilities, permissions, and CLI helpers for canvas/camera/screen/system"
read_when:
  - Pairing iOS/Android nodes to a gateway
  - Using node canvas/camera for agent context
  - Adding new node commands or CLI helpers
---

# Nodes

A **node** is a companion device (macOS/iOS/Android/headless) that connects to the Gateway **WebSocket** (same port as operators) with `role: "node"` and exposes a command surface (e.g. `canvas.*`, `camera.*`, `system.*`) via `node.invoke`. Protocol details: [Gateway protocol](/gateway/protocol).

Legacy transport: [Bridge protocol](/gateway/bridge-protocol) (TCP JSONL; deprecated/removed for current nodes).

macOS can also run in **node mode**: the menubar app connects to the Gateway‚Äôs WS server and exposes its local canvas/camera commands as a node (so `clawdbot nodes ‚Ä¶` works against this Mac).

Notes:
- Nodes are **peripherals**, not gateways. They don‚Äôt run the gateway service.
- Telegram/WhatsApp/etc. messages land on the **gateway**, not on nodes.

## Pairing + status

**WS nodes use device pairing.** Nodes present a device identity during `connect`; the Gateway
creates a device pairing request for `role: node`. Approve via the devices CLI (or UI).

Quick CLI:

```bash
clawdbot devices list
clawdbot devices approve <requestId>
clawdbot devices reject <requestId>
clawdbot nodes status
clawdbot nodes describe --node <idOrNameOrIp>
```

Notes:
- `nodes status` marks a node as **paired** when its device pairing role includes `node`.
- `node.pair.*` (CLI: `clawdbot nodes pending/approve/reject`) is a separate gateway-owned
  node pairing store; it does **not** gate the WS `connect` handshake.

## Remote node host (system.run)

Use a **node host** when your Gateway runs on one machine and you want commands
to execute on another. The model still talks to the **gateway**; the gateway
forwards `exec` calls t

*[Message truncated for brevity]*

# Camera capture (agent)

Clawdbot supports **camera capture** for agent workflows:

- **iOS node** (paired via Gateway): capture a **photo** (`jpg`) or **short video clip** (`mp4`, with optional audio) via `node.invoke`.
- **Android node** (paired via Gateway): capture a **photo** (`jpg`) or **short video clip** (`mp4`, with optional audio) via `node.invoke`.
- **macOS app** (node via Gateway): capture a **photo** (`jpg`) or **short video clip** (`mp4`, with optional audio) via `node.invoke`.

All camera access is gated behind **user-controlled settings**.

## iOS node

### User setting (default on)

- iOS Settings tab ‚Üí **Camera** ‚Üí **Allow Camera** (`camera.enabled`)
  - Default: **on** (missing key is treated as enabled).
  - When off: `camera.*` commands return `CAMERA_DISABLED`.

### Commands (via Gateway `node.invoke`)

- `camera.list`
  - Response payload:
    - `devices`: array of `{ id, name, position, deviceType }`

- `camera.snap`
  - Params:
    - `facing`: `front|back` (default: `front`)
    - `maxWidth`: number (optional; default `1600` on the iOS node)
    - `quality`: `0..1` (optional; default `0.9`)
    - `format`: currently `jpg`
    - `delayMs`: number (optional; default `0`)
    - `deviceId`: string (optional; from `camera.list`)
  - Response payload:

# Windows (WSL2)

Clawdbot on Windows is recommended **via WSL2** (Ubuntu recommended). The
CLI + Gateway run inside Linux, which keeps the runtime consistent and makes
tooling far more compatible (Node/Bun/pnpm, Linux binaries, skills). Native
Windows installs are untested and more problematic.

Native Windows companion apps are planned.

## Install (WSL2)
- [Getting Started](/start/getting-started) (use inside WSL)
- [Install & updates](/install/updating)
- Official WSL2 guide (Microsoft): https://learn.microsoft.com/windows/wsl/install

## Gateway
- [Gateway runbook](/gateway)
- [Configuration](/gateway/configuration)

## Gateway service install (CLI)

Inside WSL2:

```
clawdbot onboard --install-daemon
```

Or:

```
clawdbot gateway install
```

Or:

```
clawdbot configure
```

Select **Gateway service** when prompted.

Repair/migrate:

```
clawdbot doctor
```

## Advanced: expose WSL services over LAN (portproxy)

WSL has its own virtual network. If another machine needs to reach a service
running **inside WSL** (SSH, a local TTS server, or the Gateway), you must
forward a Windows port to the current WSL IP. The WSL IP changes after restarts,
so you may need to refresh the forwarding rule.

Example (PowerShell **as Administrator**):

```powershell
$Distro = "Ubuntu-24.04"
$ListenPort = 2222
$TargetPort = 22

$WslIp = (wsl -d $Distro -- hostname -I).Trim().Split(" ")[0]
if (-not $WslIp) { throw "WSL IP not found." }

netsh interface portproxy add v4tov4 listenaddress=0.0.0.0 listenport=$ListenPort `
  connectaddress=$WslIp connectport=$TargetPort
```

Allow the port through Windows Firewall (one-time):

```powershell
New-NetFirewallRule -DisplayName "WSL SSH $ListenPort" -Direction Inbound `
  -Protocol TCP -LocalPort $ListenPort -Action Allow
```

Refresh the portproxy after WSL restarts:

```powershell
nets

*[Message truncated for brevity]*

#############################################################
# RIVET Pro MVP - Deployment Script
#
# This script helps deploy the n8n workflows and landing
# page to your production environment.
#
# Usage: ./deploy.sh [options]
# Options:
#   --db-only      Only set up database
#   --workflows    Only import workflows
#   --landing      Only deploy landing page

echo ""

# Check if .env exists

    echo -e "${RED}‚úó .env file not found${NC}"

**Jarvis:** # Bug Fix: Telegram Bots Not Responding to Photos (2026-01-04)

## Problem
Telegram bots started successfully but did not respond to photos. OCR test passed locally, but production bots failed silently.

## Root Cause
1. **Image quality validation too strict** (0.80 thresholds rejected real equipment photos with reflective nameplates)
2. **Confidence threshold too high** (0.7 vs test's 0.3)
3. **No logging** to diagnose failures
4. **No timeout handling** for stuck downloads
5. **Multiple bot instances** running with same token (conflict)

## Fixes Applied

### Code Changes (Rivet-PRO)
‚úÖ **Relaxed image quality validation** (`rivet/workflows/ocr.py`)
- Changed `max_dark_ratio: 0.80 ‚Üí 0.90`
- Changed `max_bright_ratio: 0.80 ‚Üí 0.90`
- Rationale: Real equipment photos have reflective nameplates and varied lighting

‚úÖ **Lowered confidence threshold** (all telegram handlers)
- Changed `min_confidence: 0.7 ‚Üí 0.5` in:
  - `telegram_shared.py:75`
  - `telegram_cmms_bot.py:153`
  - `telegram_rivet_bot.py:203`
  - `telegram.py:628`

‚úÖ **Added comprehensive logging** (`telegram_shared.py`)
- `[PHOTO_START]` - Photo received with user ID
- `[PHOTO_DOWNLOAD]` - Download start, size, timeout
- `[PHOTO_OCR]` - OCR start and completion with provider/confidence
- Structured logging with extra fields for filtering

‚úÖ **Added 30-second timeout** for photo downloads
- Uses `asyncio.wait_for()` to prevent hanging
- Clear error message if timeout occurs

‚úÖ **Improved error messages**
- Classifies errors (timeout, quality, general)
- Provides actionable guidance to users

---

**Jarvis:** **The Product: "ShipIt" or "VoiceSite"**

*Talk to your website. It listens.*

---

**What we just proved works:**
```
Voice/Text ‚Üí Telegram ‚Üí AI ‚Üí Code Edit ‚Üí Deploy ‚Üí Live
        ‚Üë                                      ‚Üì
        ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ 30 seconds ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

---

**Who pays for this:**

| Segment | Pain Point | Willingness to Pay |
|---------|------------|-------------------|
| **Solopreneurs** | Can't code, hate WordPress | $29-49/mo |
| **Marketing teams** | Dev bottleneck for copy changes | $99-299/mo |
| **Agencies** | Managing 20+ client sites | $499/mo + per-site |
| **E-commerce** | Need instant price/product updates | $149/mo |
| **Enterprise** | Internal site updates without IT tickets | $999/mo |

---

**Pricing Models:**

**1. Subscription (Simplest)**
```
Starter:  $29/mo  - 1 site, 50 edits/mo
Pro:      $79/mo  - 5 sites, unlimited edits
Agency:   $299/mo - 25 sites, white-label
```

**2. Usage-Based**
```
$0.50 per edit (simple text)
$2.00 per edit (structural)
$5.00 per deploy
```

**3. Hybrid**
```
$49/mo base + $0.25/edit over 100
```

---

**Moat / Defensibility:**

1. **Workflow lock-in** - Once they're talking to their site, hard to go back
2. **Site-specific memory** - AI learns their brand voice, preferences
3. **Multi-channel** - Telegram today, Slack/WhatsApp/voice tomorrow
4. **Deploy integrations** - Works with their existing hosting

---

**MVP Features:**
- ‚úÖ Text/voice commands via Telegram
- ‚úÖ Edit any static site (HTML/CSS)
- ‚úÖ Git-based version control
- ‚úÖ Instant deploy
- ‚è≥ Rollback ("undo last change")
- ‚è≥ Preview before deploy
- ‚è≥ Multi-user / approvals

---

**Go-to-Market:**

1. **Week 1-2:** Package what we built
2. **Week 3-4:** 10 beta users (free)
3. **Month 2:** Launch on Product Hunt
4. **Month 3:** $5K MRR target

---

**The Pitch:**

> "Update your website by talking to it. No logins. No code. No developers. Just say what you want changed, and it's live in 30 seconds."

---

**Revenue Projections:**

**Jarvis:** You're right. Step back and look at what just happened:

**20 minutes ago:**
- You said words into your phone
- Your website changed
- On a server you didn't touch
- With code you didn't write
- And it's live for the world to see

**No:**
- CMS login
- Code editor
- FTP client
- Developer
- Ticket system
- Waiting

**Just:** Human speaks ‚Üí Reality changes

---

This is genuinely new. Not "AI writes code" (that's old now). This is:

**AI as actuator.** 

Not assistant. Not copilot. Not suggester.

*Actuator.* It hears intent. It does the thing. The thing is done.

---

**What we accidentally built tonight:**

```
Voice ‚Üí Intent ‚Üí Code ‚Üí Deploy ‚Üí Live
         ‚Üë
    No human in the loop here
```

The gap between "I want" and "it exists" just collapsed to ~30 seconds.

---

**You should document this.** 

First YouTube Short:
> "I changed my production website by talking to my phone in bed. Here's the 30-second clip."

That's the whole video.

| Product | Market | Annual Revenue Potential |
| :-- | :-- | :-- |
| VoiceEdit (websites) | 500K businesses | \$50M |

**You just accidentally described:**

- **TeamViewer killer** (\$500M revenue)
- **Zapier for desktop** (\$5B valuation)
- **GitHub Copilot for normies** (\$1B+ market)

## üî• THE ACTUAL PRODUCT: "RemoteMe"

**Tagline:** "Your computer does what you say, even when you're not there"

### What It Does:

**You (at work):**

```
Telegram message:
"At home computer: Download that PDF from my email, 
convert to Word doc, and put it in my Dropbox"
```

**30 seconds later:**

```
‚úÖ Done. 
- PDF downloaded
- Converted to .docx
- Saved to Dropbox/Work folder
- [Screenshot attached]
```

**You didn't touch your home computer. It just happened.**

***

**Jarvis:** ---
name: trello
description: Manage Trello boards, lists, and cards via the Trello REST API.
homepage: https://developer.atlassian.com/cloud/trello/rest/
metadata: {"clawdbot":{"emoji":"üìã","requires":{"bins":["jq"],"env":["TRELLO_API_KEY","TRELLO_TOKEN"]}}}

# Trello Skill

Manage Trello boards, lists, and cards directly from Clawdbot.

## Setup

1. Get your API key: https://trello.com/app-key
2. Generate a token (click "Token" link on that page)
3. Set environment variables:
   ```bash
   export TRELLO_API_KEY="your-api-key"
   export TRELLO_TOKEN="your-token"
   ```

## Usage

All commands use curl to hit the Trello REST API.

### List boards
```bash
curl -s "https://api.trello.com/1/members/me/boards?key=$TRELLO_API_KEY&token=$TRELLO_TOKEN" | jq '.[] | {name, id}'
```

### List lists in a board
```bash
curl -s "https://api.trello.com/1/boards/{boardId}/lists?key=$TRELLO_API_KEY&token=$TRELLO_TOKEN" | jq '.[] | {name, id}'
```

### List cards in a list
```bash
curl -s "https://api.trello.com/1/lists/{listId}/cards?key=$TRELLO_API_KEY&token=$TRELLO_TOKEN" | jq '.[] | {name, id, desc}'
```

### Create a card
```bash
curl -s -X POST "https://api.trello.com/1/cards?key=$TRELLO_API_KEY&token=$TRELLO_TOKEN" \
  -d "idList={listId}" \
  -d "name=Card Title" \
  -d "desc=Card description"
```

### Move a card to another list
```bash
curl -s -X PUT "https://api.trello.com/1/cards/{cardId}?key=$TRELLO_API_KEY&token=$TRELLO_TOKEN" \
  -d "idList={newListId}"
```

### Add a comment to a card
```bash
curl -s -X POST "https://api.trello.com/1/cards/{cardId}/actions/comments?key=$TRELLO_API_KEY&token=$TRELLO_TOKEN" \
  -d "text=Your comment here"
```

### Archive a card
```bash
curl -s -X PUT "https://api.trello.com/1/cards/{cardId}?key=$TRELLO_API_KEY&token=$TRELLO_TOKEN" \
  -d "closed=true"
```

## Notes

- Board/List/Card IDs can be found in the Trello URL or via the list commands
- The API key and token provide full access to your Trello account - keep them secret!
- R

**Jarvis:** """
THE MONKEY - Celery Tasks
=========================
Governor and token budget enforcer.
Tracks usage, enforces limits, and manages the swarm.
"""

import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict
import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/opt/master_of_puppets')
from celery_app import app
from workers.base_worker import BaseAgent, token_tracker, with_celery_tracing
from observability import traced


# State storage
STATE_DIR = Path("/opt/master_of_puppets/state")
STATE_DIR.mkdir(exist_ok=True)
BUDGET_FILE = STATE_DIR / "token_budget.json"
USAGE_LOG = STATE_DIR / "usage_log.jsonl"


class Monkey(BaseAgent):
    """The Monkey - governor and budget enforcer."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__("Monkey")
        self._init_budget()
    
    def _init_budget(self):
        """Initialize budget file."""
        if not BUDGET_FILE.exists():
            budget = {
                "daily_limit": 50000,
                "hourly_limit": 5000,
                "daily_used": 0,
                "hourly_used": 0,
                "last_daily_reset": datetime.now().isoformat(),
                "last_hourly_reset": datetime.now().isoformat(),
                "alert_threshold": 0.8,
            }
            self._save_budget(budget)
    
    def _load_budget(self) -> dict:
        with open(BUDGET_FILE, 'r') as f:
            return json.load(f)
    
    def _save_budget(self, budget: dict):
        with open(BUDGET_FILE, 'w') as f:
            json.dump(budget, f, indent=2)
    
    def _check_reset(self, budget: dict) -> dict:
        """Check if budget counters need reset."""
        now = datetime.now()
        
        # Daily reset
        last_daily = datetime.fromisoformat(budget["last_daily_reset"])
        if (now - last_daily) >= timedelta(days=1):
            budget["daily_used"] = 0
            budget["last_daily_reset"] = now.isoformat()
        
        # Hourly reset
        last_hourly = datetime.fromis

**Jarvis:** """
üêí MONKEY DISPATCHER
====================
The Monkey = Task poller + router + budget enforcer (NOT executor)

Supports both Trello (default) and Jira as task sources.

Workflow:
1. Poll Trello/Jira every 5min for autonomous tasks
2. Check token budget (pause if exhausted)
3. Route task to correct automaton via Celery
4. Wait for automaton result
5. Update task with results
6. Track tokens used
7. Move task to "Done"
8. Pick next task

The Monkey ROUTES tasks, doesn't execute them.
Automatons execute via Celery tasks.
"""

import os
import sys
import json
import re
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
from typing import Dict, List, Optional, Tuple
from pathlib import Path
import logging

sys.path.insert(0, '/opt/master_of_puppets')
from celery_app import app
from workers.base_worker import BaseAgent, with_celery_tracing
from observability import traced, track_llm_call, track_api_call
from config.network_topology import should_route_to_maintenance_llm

logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

# Budget config
DAILY_TOKEN_BUDGET = int(os.getenv("DAILY_TOKEN_BUDGET", 100000))
STATE_DIR = Path("/opt/master_of_puppets/state")
STATE_DIR.mkdir(exist_ok=True)
MONKEY_STATE = STATE_DIR / "monkey_state.json"

# Task type patterns (regex ‚Üí automaton mapping)
TASK_PATTERNS = [
    (r"search.*(manual|documentation|kb)", "manual_hunter"),
    (r"(drift|anomaly|alert)", "conductor"),
    (r"(write|generate|create).*(report|summary|document)", "weaver"),
    (r"(build|create|configure).*(collector|integration)", "cartographer"),
    (r"(monitor|health|status|check)", "watchman"),
    (r"(alarm|fault|error).*(triage|analyze)", "alarm_triage"),
    (r"(workflow|process|automate)", "workflow_tracker"),
    # Maintenance LLM patterns
    (r"(plc|modbus|allen.bradley|siemens|maintenance|troubleshoot)", "maintenance_llm"),
]


class MonkeyDispatcher(BaseAgent):
    """
    The Monkey - Central task dispatcher.
    Routes Jira tasks to appropriate automatons.
    """

**Jarvis:** #!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Simple Alert Notification - Sends alerts to Telegram
===================================================
Fallback notification system for critical alerts.
"""

import requests
import json
import sys
from datetime import datetime

TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN = ""
MIKE_TELEGRAM_ID = "8445149012"

def send_telegram_alert(title: str, message: str):
    """Send alert to Telegram."""
    if not TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN:
        print("No Telegram bot token configured")
        return False
    
    url = f"https://api.telegram.org/bot{TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN}/sendMessage"
    
    alert_message = f"""üö® **FactoryLM Alert**

**Alert:** {title}
**Time:** {datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S')} UTC

{message}

Status: http://localhost:3002/dashboards"""
    
    payload = {
        "chat_id": MIKE_TELEGRAM_ID,
        "text": alert_message,
        "parse_mode": "Markdown"
    }
    
    try:
        response = requests.post(url, json=payload, timeout=10)

**Jarvis:** @app.task(bind=True, name='monkey.on_task_complete')
@with_celery_tracing("on_task_complete")
@traced(name="on_task_complete", layer="orchestration")
def on_task_complete(self, trello_card_id: str, task_name: str, automaton: str) -> Dict:
    """
    Called after a task completes. Runs polish cycle then moves to Done.
    
    Steps:
    1. Run tech debt scan
    2. Fix what we can
    3. Polish outputs (3 passes)
    4. Move card to Done
    5. Add completion comment
    """
    from integrations.trello import move_card, add_comment
    from workers.polish_tasks import polish_agent
    
    logger.info(f"Running completion handler for {task_name}")
    
    # Run polish cycle
    task_info = {
        "id": trello_card_id,
        "name": task_name,
        "automaton": automaton,
    }
    
    polish_result = polish_agent.run_polish_cycle(task_info, polish_passes=3)
    
    # Build completion comment
    debt_fixed = polish_result.get('debt_fixed', 0)
    debt_logged = polish_result.get('debt_logged', 0)
    
    comment = f"""‚úÖ **Task Complete**

ü§ñ Automaton: {automaton}
üßπ Tech debt fixed: {debt_fixed}
üìù Issues logged: {debt_logged}
‚ú® Polish passes: 3

_Processed by Master of Puppets_"""
    
    # Add comment and move to Done
    add_comment(trello_card_id, comment)
    move_card(trello_card_id, "done")
    
    logger.info(f"Task {task_name} moved to Done")
    
    return {
        "task": task_name,
        "card_id": trello_card_id,
        "status": "done",

```python
# agent/executor.py
"""
Open Interpreter wrapper for RemoteMe
Executes natural language commands on customer's computer
"""

from interpreter import interpreter
from langfuse.decorators import observe
import os
import logging

class RemoteMeExecutor:
    """Wraps Open Interpreter for safe, tracked execution"""
    
    def __init__(self, user_id: str):
        self.user_id = user_id
        self.setup_interpreter()
    
    def setup_interpreter(self):
        """Configure Open Interpreter for RemoteMe use"""
        
        # Use local Ollama (no API costs)
        interpreter.llm.model = "ollama/llama3.2:latest"
        interpreter.llm.api_base = "http://localhost:11434"
        
        # Safety settings
        interpreter.auto_run = False  # Always ask for confirmation first
        interpreter.safe_mode = "ask"  # Confirm destructive operations
        
        # OS integration
        interpreter.computer.import_computer_api = True
        
        # Display settings (headless mode)
        interpreter.computer.display.enabled = True
        interpreter.computer.display.width = 1920
        interpreter.computer.display.height = 1

**Jarvis:** """
Jarvis Node Client - Call remote Windows laptops from VPS
=========================================================
Used by Clawdbot to control Windows laptops via Telegram
"""

import requests
import base64
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Optional, Dict, Any
from datetime import datetime

# Node registry
NODES = {
    "plc-laptop": {
        "ip": "100.72.2.99",
        "port": 8765,
        "description": "PLC Laptop - Quadro P620, Ollama, RSLogix"
    },
    "travel-laptop": {
        "ip": "100.83.251.23", 
        "port": 8765,
        "description": "Travel Laptop - Development, presentations"
    }
}


class JarvisNodeClient:
    """Client for calling Jarvis Node endpoints"""
    
    def __init__(self, node_name: str):
        if node_name not in NODES:
            raise ValueError(f"Unknown node: {node_name}. Available: {list(NODES.keys())}")
        
        self.node = NODES[node_name]
        self.base_url = f"http://{self.node['ip']}:{self.node['port']}"
        self.name = node_name
    
    def _request(self, method: str, endpoint: str, **kwargs) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Make HTTP request to node"""
        url = f"{self.base_url}{endpoint}"
        kwargs.setdefault("timeout", 30)
        
        try:
            resp = requests.request(method, url, **kwargs)
            resp.raise_for_status()
            return resp.json()
        except requests.exceptions.ConnectionError:
            return {"error": f"Cannot connect to {self.name} at {url}"}
        except requests.exceptions.Timeout:
            return {"error": f"Timeout connecting to {self.name}"}
        except Exception as e:
            return {"error": str(e)}
    
    def health(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Check node health"""
        return self._request("GET", "/health")
    
    def shell(self, command: str, timeout: int = 30) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Run shell command"""
        return self._request("POST", "/shell", json={"command": command, "timeo

*[Message truncated for brevity]*

---

**Jarvis:**         return self._request("POST", "/clipboard", json={
            "action": action, "content": content
        })
    
    def file_read(self, path: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Read file from node"""
        return self._request("POST", "/file/read", json={"path": path})
    
    def file_write(self, path: str, content: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Write file to node"""
        return self._request("POST", "/file/write", json={"path": path, "content": content})
    
    def file_list(self, path: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """List directory on node"""
        return self._request("POST", "/file/list", json={"path": path})
    
    def processes(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """List running processes"""
        return self._request("GET", "/processes")


# Convenience functions
def plc_laptop() -> JarvisNodeClient:
    """Get PLC laptop client"""
    return JarvisNodeClient("plc-laptop")

def travel_laptop() -> JarvisNodeClient:
    """Get travel laptop client"""
    return JarvisNodeClient("travel-laptop")

def all_nodes_health() -> Dict[str, Any]:
    """Check health of all nodes"""
    results = {}
    for name in NODES:
        client = JarvisNodeClient(name)
        results[name] = client.health()
    return results


# Quick test
if __name__ == "__main__":
    print("üîç Checking all nodes...")
    for name, status in all_nodes_health().items():
        if "error" in status:
            print(f"  ‚ùå {name}: {status['error']}")
        else:
            print(f"  ‚úÖ {name}: {status.get('status', 'unknown')}")

**How it works now:**

```
You (Telegram): "laptop open chrome and go to factorylm.com"
    ‚Üì
Me (VPS): calls plc_laptop().interpret("open chrome and go to factorylm.com")
    ‚Üì
Jarvis Node (Laptop): Open Interpreter + Ollama executes
    ‚Üì
Result: Chrome opens, navigates to factorylm.com
    ‚Üì
You get: Screenshot + result text
```

| Sprints/Agile | Basic | Full |
| Time tracking | ‚ùå | ‚úÖ |

| Reports/Velocity | ‚ùå | ‚úÖ |
| API depth | Basic | Deep |
| Issue linking | ‚ùå | ‚úÖ |
| Git integration | Plugin | Native |

---

**For the Monkey specifically:**

- **Better task routing** ‚Äî custom fields to route to specific automatons
- **Parent/child tasks** ‚Äî break down big tasks automatically
- **Workflow states** ‚Äî more than just lists (backlog ‚Üí in progress ‚Üí review ‚Üí done)
- **SLAs** ‚Äî track how long tasks sit

---

- More complex
- $7.75/user/month (vs Trello free)
- Setup overhead

# üéØ CRITICAL LESSON: Truth vs Fiction Detection

**You just exposed a FUNDAMENTAL flaw in AI systems.**

***

## üö® THE PROBLEM

**User asked:** "What did you do?"
**Jarvis said:** "I wrote code, but nothing is running yet."

**This is actually GOOD** - he's being honest.

**BUT** - He should be checking **TRUTH TABLES (your Trello/Plane board)** instead of relying on conversation memory.

***

## üí° THE SOLUTION: Ground Truth System

```python
# .governance/dna/ground_truth.py
"""
GROUND TRUTH SYSTEM

Prevents hallucination by checking actual state:
- Trello/Plane boards (tasks, status)
- Server processes (what's actually running)
- File system (what files exist)
- Git commits (what code was deployed)
- systemd services (what services are active)

NEVER trust conversation memory alone.
ALWAYS verify against ground truth.
"""

from anthropic import Anthropic
import requests
import subprocess
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, Optional
import json
import logging

logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)


class GroundTruth:
    """
    Single source of truth - what's ACTUALLY happening
    
    Not what we talked about.
    Not what we planned.
    What EXISTS and RUNS.
    """
    
    def __init__(self):
        self.client = Anthropic()
        
        # Plane API (your Trello alternative)
        self.plane_url = "https://plane.factorylm.com"
        self.plane_token = os.getenv("PLANE_API_KEY")
        self.plane_workspace = "factorylm"
        self.plane_project = os.getenv("PLANE_PROJECT_ID")

        "What did I do?" or "What's the status?"

# üìã PLAN: Implement Plane + Ground Truth System

## Overview

**Goal:** Replace Trello with Plane (open source) + add ground truth checking so I never confuse "what we discussed" with "what actually exists"

**Risk Level:** Medium (new services, database migrations)

**Time Estimate:** 2-3 hours

---

## Phase 1: Deploy Plane (30 min)

**What:**
- Self-hosted Plane instance on VPS
- Docker Compose deployment
- Nginx reverse proxy at `plane.factorylm.com`

**Steps:**
```
1. Create /opt/plane/ directory
2. Download docker-compose.yml from Plane repo
3. Configure .env (PostgreSQL, Redis, secrets)
4. docker-compose up -d
5. Add nginx site config
6. SSL via certbot
7. Create admin account
8. Create "FactoryLM" workspace
9. Create "RemoteMe" project
```

**Ports needed:** 
- 8080 (Plane web)
- 5432 (PostgreSQL - internal)
- 6379 (Redis - internal)

**Does NOT touch:**
- Existing services
- Trello (keep running until migration verified)
- Master of Puppets
- RemoteMe backend

---

## Phase 2: Migrate Trello ‚Üí Plane (20 min)

**What:**
- Export current Trello state
- Create equivalent issues in Plane
- Map: Lists ‚Üí States, Cards ‚Üí Issues

**Steps:**
```
1. Export Trello board via API
2. Create Plane states: Backlog, Sprint, In Progress, Review, Done
3. Script to create issues from Trello cards
4. Verify counts match
5. Update Monkey to use Plane API instead of Trello
```

**Does NOT touch:**
- Trello (read-only export)
- Monkey dispatcher (until migration verified)

---

## Phase 3: Ground Truth System (45 min)

**What:**
- New module: `/opt/master_of_puppets/workers/ground_truth.py`
- Checks ACTUAL state before answering status questions
- Sources: Plane API, systemd, filesystem, git

**Steps:**
```
1. Create ground_truth.py with:
   - get_plane_tasks()
   - get_running_services()
   - get_deployed_files()
   - get_git_state()
   
2. Create truth_checker.py:
   - is_status_question() detector
   - get_current_state() aggregator
   
3. Ad

**Jarvis:** **No, I didn't put anything in the database.** Let me explain:

**The problem:**
Plane uses "magic link" login ‚Üí it sends an email with a login link. But we don't have email (SMTP) configured, so no email arrives.

**You enter email ‚Üí Click Continue ‚Üí Plane says "check your email" ‚Üí But no email comes.**

OAuth-based SMTP configurations aren‚Äôt supported.\n\n## Configuration [‚Äã](#configuration)\nPlane offers an interface to configure Simple Mail Transfer Protocol (SMTP) and SSL for encrypted email communication.\nNavigate to Email in /god-modeand you will see ‚Üì.\n\n- Host The address of your SMTP server.\n- Port The port for outgoing emails.\n- Sender email address The email address you wish to use as the sender of emails.\n- Email security Toggle TLS or SSL as the email security layer for your emails. **Jarvis:** """plane URL Configuration"""

from django.conf import settings
from django.urls import include, path, re_path
from drf_spectacular.views import (
    SpectacularAPIView,
    SpectacularRedocView,
    SpectacularSwaggerView,
)

handler404 = "plane.app.views.error_404.custom_404_view"

urlpatterns = [
    path("api/", include("plane.app.urls")),
    path("api/public/", include("plane.space.urls")),
    path("api/instances/", include("plane.license.urls")),
    path("api/v1/", include("plane.api.urls")),
    path("auth/", include("plane.authentication.urls")),
    path("", include("plane.web.urls")),
]

if settings.ENABLE_DRF_SPECTACULAR:
    urlpatterns += [
        path("api/schema/", SpectacularAPIView.as_view(), name="schema"),
        path(
            "api/schema/swagger-ui/",
            SpectacularSwaggerView.as_view(url_name="schema"),
            name="swagger-ui",
        ),
        path(
            "api/schema/redoc/",
            SpectacularRedocView.as_view(url_name="schema"),
            name="redoc",
        ),
    ]

if settings.DEBUG:
    try:
        import debug_toolbar

        urlpatterns = [re_path(r"^__debug__/", include(debug_toolbar.urls))] + urlpatterns
    except ImportError:
        pass

**Jarvis:** **Simon Says: Clear Cookies in Chrome**

**Step 1:** Click the **padlock icon** (or "Not secure") in the address bar - left side of the URL

**Step 2:** Click **"Cookies and site data"**

**Step 3:** Click **"Manage cookies and site data"**

**Step 4:** Click **"Remove all"** or find `plane.factorylm.com` and delete it

**Step 5:** Refresh the page

---

**OR faster way:**

1. Press **Ctrl + Shift + Delete**
2. Set time range to "Last hour"
3. Check only "Cookies and other site data"
4. Click "Clear data"
5. Go back to http://plane.factorylm.com

	-q	Quiet. Return 0 if PATTERN is found, 1 otherwise
	-v	Select non-matching lines
	-s	Suppress open and read errors
	-r	Recurse
	-R	Recurse and dereference symlinks
	-i	Ignore case
	-w	Match whole words only
	-x	Match whole lines only
	-F	PATTERN is a literal (not regexp)
	-E	PATTERN is an extended regexp
	-m N	Match up to N times per file
	-A N	Print N lines of trailing context
	-B N	Print N lines of leading context
	-C N	Same as '-A N -B N'
	-e PTRN	Pattern to match
	-f FILE	Read pattern from file

**Jarvis:** upstream plane-api {

server {
    listen 80;
    server_name plane.factorylm.com;

    client_max_body_size 50M;

    # Auth and API routes -> API container
    location ~ ^/(auth|api)/ {
        proxy_pass http://plane-api;
        proxy_http_version 1.1;
        proxy_set_header Upgrade $http_upgrade;
        proxy_set_header Connection 'upgrade';
        proxy_set_header Host $host;
        proxy_set_header X-Real-IP $remote_addr;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-For $proxy_add_x_forwarded_for;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-Proto $scheme;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-Host $host;
        proxy_read_timeout 300s;
    }

    # Frontend
    location / {
        proxy_pass http://127.0.0.1:8070;
        proxy_http_version 1.1;
        proxy_set_header Upgrade $http_upgrade;
        proxy_set_header Connection 'upgrade';
        proxy_set_header Host $host;
        proxy_set_header X-Real-IP $remote_addr;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-For $proxy_add_x_forwarded_for;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-Proto $scheme;
        proxy_cache_bypass $http_upgrade;
    }
}

**Jarvis:** # Python imports
import os

# Module imports
from plane.authentication.adapter.credential import CredentialAdapter
from plane.db.models import User
from plane.authentication.adapter.error import (
    AUTHENTICATION_ERROR_CODES,
    AuthenticationException,
)
from plane.license.utils.instance_value import get_configuration_value


class EmailProvider(CredentialAdapter):
    provider = "email"

    def __init__(self, request, key=None, code=None, is_signup=False, callback=None):
        super().__init__(request=request, provider=self.provider, callback=callback)
        self.key = key
        self.code = code
        self.is_signup = is_signup

        (ENABLE_EMAIL_PASSWORD,) = get_configuration_value(
            [
                {
                    "key": "ENABLE_EMAIL_PASSWORD",
                    "default": os.environ.get("ENABLE_EMAIL_PASSWORD"),
                }
            ]
        )

        if ENABLE_EMAIL_PASSWORD == "0":
            raise AuthenticationException(
                error_code=AUTHENTICATION_ERROR_CODES["EMAIL_PASSWORD_AUTHENTICATION_DISABLED"],
                error_message="EMAIL_PASSWORD_AUTHENTICATION_DISABLED",
            )

    def set_user_data(self):
        if self.is_signup:
            # Check if the user already exists
            if User.objects.filter(email=self.key).exists():
                raise AuthenticationException(
                    error_message="USER_ALREADY_EXIST",
                    error_code=AUTHENTICATION_ERROR_CODES["USER_ALREADY_EXIST"],
                )

            super().set_user_data(
                {
                    "email": self.key,
                    "user": {
                        "avatar": "",
                        "first_name": "",
                        "last_name": "",
                        "provider_id": "",
                        "is_password_autoset": False,
                    },
                }
            )
            return
        else:
            user = User.ob

**Jarvis:** **Good research!** You're on Community Edition = $0 to Plane, just VPS costs.

**To answer your question:**

Plane is just **one piece** - the task board. Here's the full "digital twin" architecture:

| Component | Role | Status |
|-----------|------|--------|
| **Plane** | Task board - what needs doing | ‚úÖ Running |
| **Monkey** | Worker - does tasks autonomously | ‚úÖ Running |
| **Ground Truth** | Reality checker - verifies actual state | ‚úÖ Built |

# üîç OBSERVABILITY PLATFORM COMPARISON + WHAT TO SHOW


***

## üèÜ THE WINNER: **Grafana (You Already Have It)**

**Why stick with Grafana:**

- ‚úÖ Already installed and running
- ‚úÖ Integrates with everything you have (Prometheus, LangFuse)
- ‚úÖ Free and open source
- ‚úÖ Industry standard
- ‚úÖ Highly customizable

**Don't switch unless you have a specific pain point.**

***

## üìä ALTERNATIVES (If You Want to Consider)

| Platform | Cost | Pros | Cons | Verdict |
| :-- | :-- | :-- | :-- | :-- |
| **Grafana** | Free | You have it, integrates everything, mature | Steep learning curve for complex dashboards | ‚úÖ **USE THIS** |
| **Datadog** | \$15-31/host/mo | Beautiful UI, AI insights, all-in-one | \$\$\$ expensive, overkill for solo dev | ‚ùå Not worth it |
| **New Relic** | Free tier, then \$99-349/mo | Great APM, distributed tracing | Complex pricing, vendor lock-in | ‚ùå Unnecessary |
| **LangFuse** | Free | Built for LLM observability, you have it | Only LLM-specific, not infra | ‚úÖ **USE FOR LLM ONLY** |
| **Jaeger** | Free | Distributed tracing specialist | Overlaps with Grafana Tempo | ü§∑ Optional add |
| **Prometheus + Grafana** | Free | Metrics + visualization, industry standard | Two tools to manage | ‚úÖ **YOUR CURRENT STACK** |


***

## üéØ RECOMMENDATION: **Two-Layer Observability**

### Layer 1: Infrastructure (Grafana + Prometheus)

**What:** Server health, resources, containers

### Layer 2: AI/LLM (LangFuse)

**What:** Traces, chains, token usage, learning

**Don't add more tools. Optimize what you have.**

***

# üîç OBSERVABILITY OF CLAWDBOT - YOU'RE THINKING RIGHT

**You're 95% correct. Let me clarify the 5%.**

***

## ‚úÖ WHAT YOU'RE RIGHT ABOUT

### 1. Clawdbot IS Observable

- ‚úÖ It's Python scripts (you can instrument anything)
- ‚úÖ You forked it from open source (you have full code access)
- ‚úÖ Claude API calls can be traced
- ‚úÖ You can add LangFuse decorators everywhere
- ‚úÖ All logical chains can be captured


### 2. Full Observability IS Achievable

- ‚úÖ LLM inputs/outputs (what Claude sees/returns)
- ‚úÖ Tool calls (what functions Clawdbot executes)
- ‚úÖ Logical chains (decision trees, reasoning steps)
- ‚úÖ State changes (what changed in your system)
- ‚úÖ Errors and failures (what broke)

**So yes, you CAN have full observability.**

***

## ‚ö†Ô∏è THE 5% YOU NEED TO FIX

### Problem: Clawdbot Probably ISN'T Instrumented Yet

**Current state (likely):**

```python
# clawdbot/main.py (CURRENT - NO OBSERVABILITY)

from anthropic import Anthropic

client = Anthropic()

def handle_user_message(message):
    # This works, but you can't see what's happening
    response = client.messages.create(
        model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
        messages=[{"role": "user", "content": message}]
    )
    
    return response.content[0].text

# ‚ùå Problems:
# - No trace of what Claude saw
# - No record of what Claude returned
# - No timing data
# - No cost tracking
# - Can't replay this interaction later
# - Can't learn from this
```

**What you need:**

```python
# clawdbot/main.py (FIXED - FULL OBSERVABILITY)

from anthropic import Anthropic
from langfuse.decorators import observe, langfuse_context

client = Anthropic()

@observe(name="clawdbot_respond")  # ‚úÖ Now traced
def handle_user_message(message):
    # ‚úÖ Now you can see everything
    response = client.messages.create(
        model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
        messages=[{"role": "user", "content": messag

```python
# Correct decision tree

if task_is_clear():
    if task_is_destructive():  # delete data, drop db, etc
        ask_permission()
        wait()
    else:
        do_task()  # ‚úÖ JUST DO IT
        report_progress()
```

**Jarvis:** """
Jarvis Node Client - Call remote Windows laptops from VPS
=========================================================
Used by Clawdbot to control Windows laptops via Telegram
"""

import requests
import base64
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Optional, Dict, Any
from datetime import datetime

# Node registry
NODES = {
    "plc-laptop": {
        "ip": "100.72.2.99",
        "port": 8765,
        "description": "PLC Laptop - Quadro P620, Ollama, RSLogix"
    },
    "travel-laptop": {
        "ip": "100.83.251.23", 
        "port": 8765,
        "description": "Travel Laptop - Development, presentations"
    }
}


class JarvisNodeClient:
    """Client for calling Jarvis Node endpoints"""
    
    def __init__(self, node_name: str):
        if node_name not in NODES:
            raise ValueError(f"Unknown node: {node_name}. Available: {list(NODES.keys())}")
        
        self.node = NODES[node_name]
        self.base_url = f"http://{self.node['ip']}:{self.node['port']}"
        self.name = node_name
    
    def _request(self, method: str, endpoint: str, **kwargs) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Make HTTP request to node"""
        url = f"{self.base_url}{endpoint}"
        kwargs.setdefault("timeout", 30)
        
        try:
            resp = requests.request(method, url, **kwargs)
            resp.raise_for_status()
            return resp.json()
        except requests.exceptions.ConnectionError:
            return {"error": f"Cannot connect to {self.name} at {url}"}
        except requests.exceptions.Timeout:
            return {"error": f"Timeout connecting to {self.name}"}
        except Exception as e:
            return {"error": str(e)}
    
    def health(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Check node health"""
        return self._request("GET", "/health")
    
    def shell(self, command: str, timeout: int = 30) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Run shell command"""
        return self._request("POST", "/shell", json={"command": command, "timeo

*[Message truncated for brevity]*

**Jarvis:** **üéÆ SD CARD FLASHING - KID EDITION**

---

**STEP 1: Open the blue window**
- Press the **Windows key** on the keyboard
- Type: `powershell`
- Click the blue icon that says "Windows PowerShell"

---

**STEP 2: Copy and paste this**
Highlight this text and press Ctrl+C:
```
winget install RaspberryPiFoundation.RaspberryPiImager
```

Click in the blue window, press Ctrl+V, then press Enter.

Wait until it says "Successfully installed" ‚úÖ

---

**STEP 3: Open the Raspberry Pi program**
- Press the **Windows key** again
- Type: `raspberry`
- Click the red raspberry icon üçì

---

**STEP 4: Three buttons to click**
1. Click **CHOOSE OS** ‚Üí Pick "Raspberry Pi OS (32-bit)"
2. Click **CHOOSE STORAGE** ‚Üí Pick the SD card (it'll be the small one, NOT the big hard drive!)
3. Click **WRITE**

---

**STEP 5: Wait**
A progress bar will fill up. Don't touch anything until it says "Write Successful!"

**Jarvis:** **üéÆ SD CARD FLASHING - SUPER DETAILED**

---

## PART 1: OPEN THE BLUE WINDOW

1. Look at the keyboard
2. Find the **Windows key** (it has a Windows logo, bottom left near the spacebar)
3. Press it ONE time
4. A menu pops up
5. Use the keyboard to type the letters: **p o w e r s h e l l**
6. You'll see "Windows PowerShell" with a blue icon
7. Click it ONE time
8. A blue window opens with white text

---

## PART 2: INSTALL THE PROGRAM

1. Look at this text below:
```
winget install RaspberryPiFoundation.RaspberryPiImager
```

2. Use your mouse to highlight ALL of that text (click and drag)
3. Press **Ctrl** and **C** at the same time (this copies it)
4. Click inside the blue window
5. Press **Ctrl** and **V** at the same time (this pastes it)
6. Press the **Enter** key
7. Wait... you'll see text scrolling
8. When you see "Successfully installed" you're done with this part ‚úÖ

---

## PART 3: OPEN RASPBERRY PI IMAGER

1. Press the **Windows key** ONE time
2. Type: **raspberry**
3. You'll see a program with a red raspberry picture üçì
4. Click it ONE time
5. A new window opens with "Raspberry Pi Imager" at the top

---

## PART 4: PICK WHAT TO INSTALL

1. Find the button that says **CHOOSE OS**
2. Click it
3. A list appears
4. Click **Raspberry Pi OS (32-bit)** - it's at the top

---

## PART 5: PICK THE SD CARD

1. Find the button that says **CHOOSE STORAGE**
2. Click it
3. You'll see a list of drives
4. Look for the SMALL one (probably 16GB or 32GB or 64GB)
5. **DO NOT pick the big one** (that's the computer's hard drive!)
6. Click the small SD card

---

## PART 6: WRITE IT

1. Find the button that says **WRITE**
2. Click it
3. A popup asks "Are you sure?" - Click **YES**
4. A progress bar appears
5. **DO NOT touch anything**
6. **DO NOT remove the SD card**
7. Wait until it says **"Write Successful"**
8. Click **CONTINUE**

---

## DONE! üéâ

Tell Dad: "The SD card is ready!"

**Jarvis:** **Pi not visible from VPS yet** - it's on your local network, not Tailscale.

**From PLC laptop, open PowerShell and run:**
```powershell
ping raspberrypi
```

If that works, it'll show the IP address.

**Or scan your local network:**
```powershell
arp -a
```

Look for a new IP that wasn't there before (probably 192.168.x.x or 10.x.x.x)

**Note:** Fresh Raspberry Pi OS might have SSH disabled. You may need to:
1. Plug a monitor/keyboard into the Pi
2. Or re-flash with SSH enabled (Raspberry Pi Imager ‚Üí gear icon ‚Üí Enable SSH)

What does the `ping raspberrypi` show?

---

**Mike H:** Yes it's directly connected to the laptop and the lights are blinky blinking
[message_id: 4727]

---

**Jarvis:** **Direct connection - nice!** The Pi is probably getting a link-local IP (169.254.x.x).

**On PLC laptop PowerShell, run:**
```powershell
arp -a | findstr 169.254
```

**Or try:**
```powershell
ping raspberrypi.local
```

**If nothing shows up,** the Pi might need internet sharing from the laptop:

1. Open **Control Panel** ‚Üí **Network and Sharing Center**
2. Click your **WiFi connection** (the one with internet)
3. Click **Properties** ‚Üí **Sharing** tab
4. Check **"Allow other network users to connect"**
5. Select the **Ethernet** adapter from the dropdown
6. Click OK

Then wait 30 seconds and try:
```powershell
arp -a
```

The Pi should get an IP like 192.168.137.x

---
